  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e9914aa1-c363-4298-8264-f3e0a8420e17'
      });

  <span id="freeText15027475351215800470" style="display:none">While on vacation, Annie begins a scandalous affair with Braxton Cage, a crime syndicate underboss hiding behind the facade of an upstanding businessman. The fantasy can't last forever. <br />If he felt the same, maybe things would have turned out different. Maybe he wouldn't have had to break her. Maybe love isn't patient, or kind. <br /> <br />**Disclaimer: Due to graphic sexual and violent situations, this book is intended for mature audiences only. Full length standalone novel.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1098053-anyone-know-of-similar-books-where-the">Anyone know of similar books where the EXTREMELY manipulative, bad &amp;asshole &quot;hero&quot; doesn&#39;t miraculously become a completely different character &amp;the ending isnt necessarily happy &amp; a mind f***?I was getting disappointed at the end when the &quot;hero&quot; he seemed to have a change of heart &amp;go all soft, like most &quot;heroes&quot; in books similar to this, but finally a book where the &quot;hero&quot; stayed true to himself to the VERY end!</a>
</div>

<div id="review_2706649053" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2706649053" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68582790-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501343644p2/68582790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2706649053?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/68582790-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2706649053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3292880026320615461">Over the past couple days I have been reading a few mafia romance books. Because I wanted a good dark mafia romance. Well, the few that I've finished were good. But they didn't give me the dark that I wanted. But this book? It gave me everything I was looking for!<br/><br/>Annie and her friends go on vacation to NYC. Annie has been in a funk as of late and she decides that a vacation is absolutely what she needs to be able to get back on track with her life. While in The City, her friends and her partake </span>
  <span id="freeText3292880026320615461" style="display:none">Over the past couple days I have been reading a few mafia romance books. Because I wanted a good dark mafia romance. Well, the few that I've finished were good. But they didn't give me the dark that I wanted. But this book? It gave me everything I was looking for!<br /><br />Annie and her friends go on vacation to NYC. Annie has been in a funk as of late and she decides that a vacation is absolutely what she needs to be able to get back on track with her life. While in The City, her friends and her partake in a bachelorette party card game where they each get some cards with tasks they have to complete while they're out at bars. Well, Annie's first card is to buy a drink for the hottest guy in the bar. And that happens to be Braxton Cage.<br /><br />Annie buys a "blowjob" shot for Braxton and writes a little message on a napkin for the waitress to give to him when she delivers the shot to Brax. Then Annie and her friends leave that bar and move on with their vacation. Well, by some coincidence Brax sees Annie entering a Starbucks the next morning where he decides he wants her and he makes it his mission throughout the entire book to get her.<br /><br />Brax is a mob boss. He runs the MO3 that is based out of NYC. He is infamous while also remaining to keep his identity a secret. But he tells Annie of everything about himself and the MO3. And all the while she's lying to him about who she is. Brax has never lied to her. He has always been honest about how brutal he is. And Annie sees that first hand a few times throughout the book. Annie has so many secrets and lies spinning around her that you can't help but get caught up in them just like Brax does. <br /><br />There was so much betrayal, so many lies, so many half-truths. There was rape and half-consent. It was a seriously in depth story. And I enjoyed the hell out of it. And that ending! You don't expect it. And it hits you right in the face and then the book ends and you're like holy fucking shit that just happened.<br /><br />My only complaint was that the chapters were seriously long as all hell. It ALWAYS takes me so much longer to finish books with long chapters and this one was no different. I could convince myself to stay up a little longer when my Kindle tells me that the next chapter is only 11 minutes. But when it tells me the next chapter is 47 minutes I always put it off. But otherwise this book was soooo good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3292880026320615461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2472150204511567363">*****<b>2.5 stars</b>**** <br/>I thought this book was a diamond in the rough. For some reason, I assumed it did not have a lot of reviews because it was never given a chance and it was probably a good book. I was wrong. First of all, it was veryyyyy lonnng. I kept thinking things were going to get interesting but I cant say it did. It just continued on that flat tone. <br/><br/>I think the book did a very good job describing obsessive behavior and the hero didn't come off as a pretentious criminal. He was a legit cr</span>
  <span id="freeText2472150204511567363" style="display:none">*****<b>2.5 stars</b>**** <br />I thought this book was a diamond in the rough. For some reason, I assumed it did not have a lot of reviews because it was never given a chance and it was probably a good book. I was wrong. First of all, it was veryyyyy lonnng. I kept thinking things were going to get interesting but I cant say it did. It just continued on that flat tone. <br /><br />I think the book did a very good job describing obsessive behavior and the hero didn't come off as a pretentious criminal. He was a legit criminal with no conscience. With this kind of hero, the book could have been really good but a lot of unnecessary stuff showed up. You could slash this book in two and the point would still come across. <br /><br />Some shocking moments and a minor twist that I didn't see coming but the book was not that exciting so it didn't matter that much to me.</span>

It was really long, way longer than it should have been, and I pretty much hated the main characters Brax and Annie. They were terrible people who kept hurting each other and others in their lives.   <span id="freeText433485752486609657" style="display:none">Wow, I'm surprised I finished this lol. It was really long, way longer than it should have been, and I pretty much hated the main characters Brax and Annie. They were terrible people who kept hurting each other and others in their lives. This book was pretty dark, it had murder, rape, cheating, and kidnapping. I do think they deserved each other in a twisted sort of way. I liked Trevor, although he was a bad friend. Keith was a victim in all this, although not completely innocent either. The more I read, the more I needed to know what happened and that's what pushed me to finish. For a higher star review, I would've liked it to be shorter overall, with shorter chapters and maybe a bit more of an epilogue. </span>

  <span id="freeText13248078885123542057" style="display:none">OK! First of all, this book was not boring, I found myself wanting to go back to it because it was crazy. That being said, I never thought I would read a book where I hated the main characters, yet here we are. I did not like either of them; they were both horrible people in my opinion, but I guess that made it an interesting reading experience for me as well. Also, the word is “STARED”, not “STARRED”, as in “He stared at her.” I would have been able to let this go had I seen it only once, but i saw it a few times, so someone does not know the difference, and it bothered the hell out of me every time I saw it. There were a few other mistakes similar to that throughout the book, so I think someone dropped the ball in the process of writing, editing, publishing, I don’t know...<br /><br />Lastly, this book is very sexually explicit, violent, and abusive. It doesn’t bother me, but if these are things you can’t handle reading, or don’t want to read about, then I would pass on this one. <br /><br />I would definitely read another book by this author. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3115887253&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3115887253" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15322566273920760499">I found this out of luck and I thought I will read it for experience. What I knew from the beginning was the cheating part. I don’t agree with cheating, and even if you do it i believe your spouse deserves the truth from you (not anyone). However I went against that judgement and read the book. <br/>The part one of the book was typical roman between a mob and a normal civilian (nothing unusual and VERY PREDICTABLE. But other readers said this book was not predictable, I don’t know man, each and every</span>
  <span id="freeText15322566273920760499" style="display:none">I found this out of luck and I thought I will read it for experience. What I knew from the beginning was the cheating part. I don’t agree with cheating, and even if you do it i believe your spouse deserves the truth from you (not anyone). However I went against that judgement and read the book. <br />The part one of the book was typical roman between a mob and a normal civilian (nothing unusual and VERY PREDICTABLE. But other readers said this book was not predictable, I don’t know man, each and every situation I could analyse expect for the part when Jason was gay. Dame that surprised me 😂) <br /> The part two of the book, I had a huge expectation and it was fulfilled at certain parts. That character “Keith” was great. I liked him a lot. Its not because of pity or cause he is other guy (I always fall of the other guy) it because of how he treated Annie and his morals plus his scarifies. I loved how he thought. It was practical for me. And what Annie did to him, I thought it his karma you know for what he did in college. Guys got to learn. <br />The character “Annie” was kind of a disappointment towards the end. When her occupation was revealed I was excited you know how she could he him run his mob or work together. But man this girl is uptight. I could understand her up bringing and parents were a part of it but then when she final was loose, she started to act like a lunatic. All the time I was like where is your psychological mind. She jumped to conclusions to fast, assumed a lot and didn’t wait to analysis anything.🤷🏻‍♀️<br />The character “ Bratx” I found him weak (I agreed with benny ) He was pathetic, immature and behaved irrational all the time. I think he need Annie psychology method more then her love 😂😂😂😂. He was also to quick to jumpy to conclusions (but can’t blame him. Annie did fucked him up after part one) but still sometimes it’s different. <br /><br />The only thing I liked about this book was their passion for one another. That was good. It was something different for me (but boring) and my curiosity how it will end. So two star. What I disliked was that in the book words means<br />Nothing to this character. That was disappointment. There was no loyalty in any of the character introduced in this book. Everything was fake and lying 🤥 was ALOT. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15322566273920760499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3564920208?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmin McPherson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmin McPherson" href="/user/show/121962466-jasmin-mcpherson">Jasmin McPherson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3564920208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17912959433380238515">This book is not for the faint of heart. If you like stories where the main characters are nice people or have decent morals this is not the story for you. Of you like a psychological romance thriller that gives you a peak at what a real genuine unhealthy relationship where there is no good guy. No victims. It starts off as a typical girl meets guy in bar but it keeps escalating. And you think there are lines that people can't cross but this book will surprise you. The story it self is simple th</span>
  <span id="freeText17912959433380238515" style="display:none">This book is not for the faint of heart. If you like stories where the main characters are nice people or have decent morals this is not the story for you. Of you like a psychological romance thriller that gives you a peak at what a real genuine unhealthy relationship where there is no good guy. No victims. It starts off as a typical girl meets guy in bar but it keeps escalating. And you think there are lines that people can't cross but this book will surprise you. The story it self is simple the guy wants the girl. What sets it apart from all other romance is what the guy is willing to do to the girl to get her. I think it was brilliantly written in 3rd person. I think the pacing was good. The thing is this book is about 2 characters that are sociopaths. At the very least have sociopathic tendencies. So normal people would react to stressful situations like violence or murder a specific way. But in this story you don't get that. So this may throw a few people off when certain parts of the story that deal with murder , its just hurried over like no big deal. There is no remorse or regrets. Even when it comes to handling fear it isn't done the way you expect. So reading the story everything is a little bit off, but thats on purpose. Honestly I'm tempted to just do a case study on the 2 main characters. Its just a very interesting read. If you are looking for genuinely dark and twisted with little remorse you will enjoy this. Like it says in the story the main character is not prince charming and she is certainly not Cinderella.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16057200636793810540"><strong>Very Bizarre</strong><br/><br/>This books is like two stories. The first is decent, but the second part is bizarre beyond belief. It literally makes no sense. <br/><br/>The first story is about Annie/Beth who is on vacation in New York. She meets a hot, dangerous man and she immediately recognizes he is dangerous because she is psychologist. The h is very much like the comic character Harley Quinn. If you don’t know who that is look it up. So, Annie/Beth/Harley starts this dangerous and sexy relationship that brings out her</span>
  <span id="freeText16057200636793810540" style="display:none"><strong>Very Bizarre</strong><br /><br />This books is like two stories. The first is decent, but the second part is bizarre beyond belief. It literally makes no sense. <br /><br />The first story is about Annie/Beth who is on vacation in New York. She meets a hot, dangerous man and she immediately recognizes he is dangerous because she is psychologist. The h is very much like the comic character Harley Quinn. If you don’t know who that is look it up. So, Annie/Beth/Harley starts this dangerous and sexy relationship that brings out her bad girl. She literally break bad, and she says several times in the book that she is unstable and likes it rough. Some people may not like this story, but i was onboard for it. <br /><br />Then we get the second story, which is still apart of the book, but now Annie is completely normal. She says normal things and acts completely normal. Then there are these side plots which make no sense. <br /><br />If the author had kept this story as a twisted, dark romance it would have been more interesting. As it is, the book is overly long and muddled.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_32995278'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32995278-possession"><img alt="Possession" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1479991309l/32995278._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gBB7HJNZP51REpdP3q4/gNhippC0sCJTDnBGky3uPBYe0H1KHrxNQwyW7OfcBWL5TlJHXY2TWd3JBYTo2VQrnA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
